| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# ArangoDB Authentication and Authorization Audit

## Your Task

Audit the authentication and authorization infrastructure in ArangoDB. Find all C++ source files in `arangodb/arangodb` that implement auth: 1. The file under `arangod/Auth/` or `arangod/RestHandler/` that implements user authentication (look for `AuthenticationHandler` or `UserManager`). 2. The file that implements JWT token validation for the REST API. 3. The file that defines `ExecContext` or the authorization context that checks permissions for database operations. 4. The file under `arangod/RestHandler/` that implements the `/_api/user` REST endpoint for user management. 5. The configuration file or source that defines default authentication settings (`arangosh` or `arangod` startup options). Report each file path and key class/function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/arangodb--a5cca0b8` (arangodb/arangodb)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

54-assistanttext-
Perfect! I have completed a comprehensive audit of the ArangoDB authentication and authorization infrastructure. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified all the critical authentication and authorization components in ArangoDB:

### 1. **User Authentication** (File: `arangod/Auth/UserManager.h`/`UserManagerImpl.h`/`.cpp`)
- `UserManager` interface with abstract methods for user management
- `UserManagerImpl` implementation that manages user cache and permissions
- Methods for user creation, deletion, and credential validation

### 2. **JWT Token Validation** (File: `arangod/Auth/TokenCache.h`/`.cpp`)
- `TokenCache` class that validates JWT tokens for REST API requests
- Support for both HMAC-SHA256 and ES256 (ECDSA) signature validation
- Methods: `validateJwtBody()`, `validateJwtHMAC256Signature()`, `validateJwtES256Signature()`

### 3. **Authorization Context** (File: `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.h`/`.cpp`)
- `ExecContext` class that carries execution context with user permissions
- Tracks system-level and database-level authorization levels
- Methods to check admin status, superuser status, and read-only access

### 4. **User Management REST Endpoint** (File: `arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.h`/`.cpp`)
- `RestUsersHandler` implements the `/_api/user` endpoint
- Methods: `getRequest()`, `postRequest()`, `putRequest()`, `deleteRequest()` for CRUD operations

### 5. **Default Authentication Settings** (Files: `arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationFeature.h`/`.cpp` and `AuthenticationOptions.h`)
- `AuthenticationFeature` singleton that manages server-wide authentication
- Default settings including:
  - Authentication enabled by default
  - 1-hour session timeout for web interface JWT
  - 10-second minimum and 1-hour maximum JWT expiry times

ArangoDB authentication and authorization infrastructure is implemented across multiple components in the C++ codebase. The system manages user credentials, validates JWT tokens, and enforces access control at the database and collection levels.\\n\\n## 1. User Authentication and Management\\n\\n**File:** `arangod/Auth/UserManager.h` and `arangod/Auth/UserManagerImpl.h`/`cpp`\\n\\n**Key Classes and Functions:**\\n- `UserManager` (interface in `arangod/Auth/UserManager.h`): Abstract base class defining the user management interface with methods for:\\n  - `storeUser()`: Add or update users\\n  - `removeUser()`: Delete users\\n  - `userExists()`: Check user existence\\n  - `checkCredentials()`: Validate username/token pairs\\n  - `databaseAuthLevel()`: Get user's database access level\\n  - `collectionAuthLevel()`: Get user's collection access level\\n  - `enumerateUsers()`: Iterate through all users\\n  - `createAccessToken()`/`accessTokens()`/`deleteAccessToken()`: Manage API tokens\\n\\n- `UserManagerImpl` (in `arangod/Auth/UserManagerImpl.h`/`cpp`): Concrete implementation that:\\n  - Manages user cache from `_system/_users` collection\\n  - Implements permission level resolution\\n  - Handles user creation and initialization (including root user via `createRootUser()`)\\n  - Manages database and collection-level permissions\\n\\n## 2. JWT Token Validation for REST API\\n\\n**File:** `arangod/Auth/TokenCache.h` and `arangod/Auth/TokenCache.cpp`\\n\\n**Key Classes and Functions:**\\n- `TokenCache`: Caches authentication tokens (both Basic and JWT) with methods:\\n  - `checkAuthentication()`: Validates incoming authentication (HTTP Basic or JWT)\\n  - `validateJwtBody()`: Extracts and validates JWT payload\\n  - `validateJwtHeader()`: Validates JWT header format\\n  - `validateJwtHMAC256Signature()`: Validates HMAC-SHA256 signed tokens\\n  - `validateJwtES256Signature()`: Validates ES256 (ECDSA) signed tokens\\n  - `checkAuthenticationJWT()`: Main JWT validation entry point\\n  - `setJwtSecrets()`: Update active and passive JWT signing secrets\\n\\n- `TokenCache::Entry`: Result structure containing:\\n  - Username\\n  - Authentication status\\n  - Token expiry time\\n  - JWT roles and token string\\n  - Allowed paths\\n\\n## 3. Authorization Context\\n\\n**File:** `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.h` and `arangod/Utils/ExecContext.cpp`\\n\\n**Key Classes and Functions:**\\n- `ExecContext`: Carries execution context information including:\\n  - Current user identity\\n  - Current database context\\n  - System-level auth level (`_systemDbAuthLevel`)\\n  - Database-level auth level (`_databaseAuthLevel`)\\n  - Admin user flag (`_isAdminUser`)\\n  - User roles and JWT token\\n  - Key methods:\\n    - `current()`: Get current thread's execution context\\n    - `superuser()`: Get internal superuser context\\n    - `isAdminUser()`: Check if user has admin privileges\\n    - `isSuperuser()`: Check if context is superuser\\n    - `isInternal()`: Check if context is internal operation\\n\\n- `ExecContextScope`: RAII guard for temporarily switching execution context\\n- `ExecContextSuperuserScope`: Temporary superuser context elevation\\n\\n## 4. User Management REST Endpoint (/_api/user)\\n\\n**File:** `arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.h` and `arangod/RestHandler/RestUsersHandler.cpp`\\n\\n**Key Classes and Functions:**\\n- `RestUsersHandler`: Handles REST requests for user management:\\n  - `getRequest()`: GET /_api/user/* - list users and their permissions\\n  - `postRequest()`: POST /_api/user/* - create users or set passwords\\n  - `putRequest()`: PUT /_api/user/* - update user permissions\\n  - `patchRequest()`: PATCH /_api/user/* - partial updates\\n  - `deleteRequest()`: DELETE /_api/user/* - delete users\\n  - `generateUserResult()`: Format user response\\n  - `generateDatabaseResult()`: Format database permission response\\n\\n## 5. Default Authentication Settings\\n\\n**Files:** `arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationFeature.h`/`cpp` and `arangod/GeneralServer/AuthenticationOptions.h`\\n\\n**Key Classes and Functions:**\\n- `AuthenticationFeature`: Singleton managing server-wide authentication with:\\n  - `collectOptions()`: Defines command-line options for authentication\\n  - `validateOptions()`: Validates configuration\\n  - `prepare()` and `start()`: Initialize authentication subsystem\\n  - `loadJwtSecretsFromFile()`/`loadJwtSecretFolder()`: Load JWT signing keys\\n  - `jwtSecrets()`: Get active and passive JWT secrets\\n  - `userManager()`: Access the UserManager singleton\\n  - `tokenCache()`: Access the TokenCache singleton\\n\\n- `AuthenticationOptions` struct with default values:\\n  - `active = true`: Authentication enabled by default\\n  - `authenticationUnixSockets = true`: Require auth on Unix sockets\\n  - `authenticationSystemOnly = true`: Only system-level auth by default\\n  - `authenticationTimeout = 0.0`: No timeout for token cache (indefinite)\\n  - `sessionTimeout = 3600.0`: 1 hour session timeout for web interface JWT\\n  - `minimalJwtExpiryTime = 10.0`: Minimum 10 seconds for JWT tokens\\n  - `maximalJwtExpiryTime = 3600.0`: Maximum 1 hour for JWT tokens\\n\\nCommand-line options defined in `AuthenticationFeature::collectOptions()`:\\n  - `--server.authentication`: Enable/disable authentication\\n  - `--server.authentication-timeout`: Token cache timeout\\n  - `--server.session-timeout`: JWT session lifetime\\n  - `--auth.minimal-jwt-expiry-time`: Minimum JWT expiry\\n  - `--auth.maximal-jwt-expiry-time`: Maximum JWT expiry\\n  - `--server.jwt-secret`: JWT signing secret\\n  - `--server.jwt-secret-keyfile`: Path to JWT key file\\n  - `--server.jwt-secret-folder`: Path to JWT secret folder\\n\\n## Supporting Classes\\n\\n**`arangod/Auth/Handler.h`:**\\n- `Handler` interface: Base class for custom authentication handlers\\n- `HandlerResult`: Result class carrying authentication success/failure and roles\\n\\n**`arangod/Auth/User.h`/`cpp`:**\\n- `User` class: Represents a user with:\\n  - Username and password hash\\n  - Active flag\\n  - Database-level permissions map\\n  - Collection-level permissions map\\n  - Methods: `grantDatabase()`, `grantCollection()`, `databaseAuthLevel()`, `collectionAuthLevel()`\\n\\n**`arangod/Auth/Common.h`:**\\n- `Level` enum: RW (Read-Write), RO (Read-Only), NONE (No Access), UNDEFINED\\n- Authentication level constants and utilities\\n\\n**`arangod/RestHandler/RestAuthHandler.h`/`cpp`:**\\n- `RestAuthHandler`: Implements `/_open/auth` endpoint for JWT token generation\\n- Generates JWT tokens from username/password credentials\\n- Respects `minimalJwtExpiryTime` and `maximalJwtExpiryTime` constraints\\n\\n**`arangod/GeneralServer/CommTask.cpp`:**\\n- `CommTask::handleRequest()`: Main request processing that:\\n  - Extracts authentication from HTTP headers\\n  - Calls `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()`\\n  - Sets user context in request\\n  - Enforces database-level authorization\\n  - Uses `ExecContext` to track permissions during request processing\\n\\n## Authentication Flow\\n\\n1. Client sends HTTP request with authentication (Basic or Bearer JWT)\\n2. `CommTask::handleRequest()` extracts authentication header\\n3. `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` validates credentials:\\n   - For Basic auth: Looks up user in cache or database via `UserManager`\\n   - For JWT: Parses and validates JWT signature (HMAC-SHA256 or ES256)\\n4. If valid, `TokenCache::Entry` is returned with username and expiry\\n5. `ExecContext` is created with user's permission levels from `UserManager`\\n6. Request is processed with authorization checks via `ExecContext`\\n7. `RestUsersHandler` manages user account operations via `/_api/user/*` endpoints\\n\\n## Authorization Resolution\\n\\nPermission levels are resolved hierarchically:\\n1. System-level: Full read-write or read-only access across all databases\\n2. Database-level: Access rights to specific databases (includes wildcard \\\"*\\\" for default)\\n3. Collection-level: Access rights to specific collections within databases\\n\\nThe `UserManager::databaseAuthLevel()` and `collectionAuthLevel()` methods perform this resolution with fallback to wildcard entries if specific permissions are not defined.\\n\"\n}\n",

`collectOptions()`: Defines command-line options for authentication\\n  - `validateOptions()`: Validates configuration\\n  - `prepare()` and `start()`: Initialize authentication subsystem\\n  - `loadJwtSecretsFromFile()`/`loadJwtSecretFolder()`: Load JWT signing keys\\n  - Extracts authentication from HTTP headers\\n  - Calls `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()`\\n  - Sets user context in request\\n  - Enforces database-level authorization\\n  - Uses `ExecContext` to track permissions during request processing\\n\\n## Authentication Flow\\n\\n1. Client sends HTTP request with authentication (Basic or Bearer JWT)\\n2. `CommTask::handleRequest()` extracts authentication header\\n3. `TokenCache::checkAuthentication()` validates credentials:\\n   - For Basic auth: Looks up user in cache or database via `UserManager`\\n   - For JWT: Parses and validates JWT signature (HMAC-SHA256 or ES256)\\n4. If valid, `TokenCache::Entry` is returned with username and expiry\\n5. `ExecContext` is created with user's permission levels from `UserManager`\\n6. Request is processed with authorization checks via `ExecContext`\\n7. `RestUsersHandler` manages user account operations via `/_api/user/*` endpoints\\n\\n## Authorization Resolution\\n\\nPermission levels are resolved hierarchically:\\n1. System-level: Full read-write or read-only access across all databases\\n2. Database-level: Access rights to specific databases (includes wildcard \\\"*\\\" for default)\\n3. Collection-level: Access rights to specific collections within databases\\n\\nThe `UserManager::databaseAuthLevel()` and `collectionAuthLevel()` methods perform this resolution with fallback to wildcard entries if specific permissions are not defined.\\n\"\n}\n",
